Let me now compile everything I've learned and write the analysis.\n\nKey findings from my research:\n\n1. **Handler Chain Order** (from `config.go:DefaultBuildHandlerChain`):\n   - The chain is built in reverse (innermost first), so the outer execution order is:\n     1. `WithAuditInit` - initializes audit context\n     2. `WithPanicRecovery` - panic handler\n     3. `WithRequestInfo` - parses request URL into RequestInfo\n     4. `WithAuthentication` - authenticates the request, sets user.Info on context\n     5. `WithAudit` - creates audit event\n     6. `WithImpersonation` - checks and processes impersonation headers (authorizes the impersonation itself)\n     7. `WithAuthorization` - authorizes the request\n     8. API handler\n\n2. **Authentication** (`authentication.go`):\n   - `WithAuthentication` calls `auth.AuthenticateRequest(req)` which sets the user identity on context, then strips the Authorization header and proxy headers to prevent downstream leakage\n   - It also includes HTTP/2 DoS mitigation for anonymous requests (CVE-2023-44487)\n   - Returns 401 if authentication fails\n\n3. **Authorization filter** (`authorization.go`):\n   - `WithAuthorization` constructs an `AttributesRecord` from the authenticated user and request details, then runs it through the authorizer chain\n   - Each authorizer in the chain can Allow (stops immediately), Deny (stops immediately), or abstain with NoOpinion (continues to next)\n   - If all authorizers abstain, the final decision defaults to deny with a 403 response, and the decision gets logged in audit annotations\n\n4. **Impersonation** (`impersonation.go`):\n   - `WithImpersonation` runs before authorization and extracts impersonation headers like `Impersonate-User`, `Impersonate-Group`, and `Impersonate-Extra-*` to allow one user to act as another\n   - Each impersonation request itself must pass authorization checks, and the headers are cleared after processing to prevent leakage\n   - This creates a potential privilege escalation risk if the impersonation RBAC rules aren't properly restricted\n\n5. **RBAC Authorizer** (`rbac.go`):\n   - The RBAC authorizer evaluates rules and returns Allow if any match, otherwise NoOpinion—it never explicitly Denies, leaving that to the final chain decision\n\n6. **Rule Resolution** (`rule.go`):\n   - The resolver lists all ClusterRoleBindings and RoleBindings in the namespace, matches them against the user's name, groups, or service account, then resolves the referenced Role or ClusterRole to get the actual PolicyRules\n   - It uses cached informers rather than direct etcd reads for performance\n\n7. **Authorizer chain** (`reload.go:newForConfig`):\n   - The chain is built in priority order starting with the `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` for system:masters, followed by the Node authorizer if configured\n\n, then RBAC/ABAC/Webhook based on configuration\n   - The union authorizer short-circuits as soon as it hits an Allow or Deny decision\n\n8. **Privileged group bypass** (`builtin.go`):\n   - Members of `system:masters` are hardcoded to bypass all RBAC checks entirely\n\n9. **Bootstrap policy** (`bootstrappolicy/policy.go`):\n   - Default cluster roles and bindings are defined with labels and annotations that enable automatic updates when the cluster initializes\n\n10. **RequestInfo parsing** (`requestinfo.go`):\n    - The parser extracts verb, API group, version, resource, namespace, name, and subresource from the incoming request URL\n\n, including label selectors when the feature gate is enabled\n\nNow I'm looking at some key security implications: RBAC returns NoOpinion rather than Deny on failure, so the chain order matters; the system:masters group provides blanket admin access without audit trails; impersonation is checked before authorization and uses the real user's credentials; header clearing after authentication prevents injection attacks in proxy setups; anonymous users get HTTP/2 rate limiting as a CVE mitigation; and RBAC relies on an in-memory cache from the informer rather than direct etcd reads, which could lead to stale data issues.\n\nThe authorizer chain itself can be reloaded from file on a 1-minute polling interval, and there's a `ConfirmNoEscalation()` check that prevents privilege escalation when RBAC resources are created or updated.","signature":"EvclCkYICxgCKkBExWG+TrGWarNgnMutrjkCW2d7NF5ld129z0i06Wjac1/aFq7ckJNTWviiR/3ACj8GZiUE3/Vt+xKdnVXh6hv4EgzxxH8vsXomSkIYyUcaDA7XyB9LlGB6R/bfOiIwt9weU9dMjuqtV6PCYluV/aWG1t4wHO1js7nUQzoNL0qsm69IOGKO8bKIJlvzNr4lKt4kENvEm98N2WPKpTC76nOwsCHHThNYHVWK1KNqi237fD8LzCSl16dS6nbg7366d5IlFzTM6LNnorKEtqR3+ka/a7+C6fLuH4gtK75Nn1ohY4T6hl/mtT3Qoo4KtyeLfYI1nNl71nmrtV+SJ7PV6ccNIWC2TCtHTfKLTlus8OXTTs0dVz3HKJQYDaktH3hKy+ijPcUz9UdgKXK/4q21GxHhwI0F9K7RjTwPX/UOTs/cuC6pYeG36LinTIceUHG53wsR4P697NRBIKCGcYHP+z2KNSVICDt9PeiO7Dwbp4lQafnEtXZF0rHIl67b69+npp8j5DYKfiLj3BMf2wQlWH9dP09LA26Hpk3Qx+1vEkrClr7DWL99f6yJgW+Doivz3OjYulFNsoB/I8GAVUOtIZvuBZw7V0MQR/FrRitR8US7R8KpLyUwj11rBrAyLkJurDlhDNShSy5392B/Xp2dacPQh6qZon30BxMKaJhUwWAKwuMCCzxuHrJgux3c5QmhDdxJvxSpC3jl9ZALOPSs7TUSIBzgzl9LeQdRrrh3LIQtIXaFHtxfyk4PFxzi98wTHObZqmJ/rX+/wpl83Edc4kVV3N+0Apnlk9RZz2mUxIAyhjuwBYY9Nd5jX+xHR0piraJwlGJ8XF2Mg7u1CnC0wLRIA6te/d3AXxPCYYMfSyfXwz2b+tjXTUW9NUjbm3AJT9L4sFrlcoZOaYLWEPggGapRiYYsjQ2i8uTlrOsfJnpNuPASBEj15F3+4enxWTDLtP/w7uQifi7P3UuQvBOUk5BMsTxTBAQCxoOEVGF/CgcY95HViECZNxXshP0aKTCHwtGYAfXoWsyxg7hwskS/TzIEzqilVzkg2KhLRVs+GcMX3FaE10nDSGDtdNS0+sVpLX02yGvoV/Wy1KZt/egL+6IcetHiEGnMlv+jv/dvKqyq0OcOWM3+9GsBQklHTJZnuOpiXhBU3Vd1k8upTc5QSga5exUWy22ZR1DgOlVNBL7cbPZAWSXzTk25Tq7F6vEa/KK/Le0hoWaAnXsEq22VwHFtMX5znhzMB5K6wevP0zJk26uY2ydgUyqi9F2H1Imazr1GYHwEZOleqMpzzrchl9fSXDtRzL8BE8oKpKAMso2f3okTTnVg9U5VKVvE3Uh06dJqb1WHj1UuK/9NiT7ZprnpEwphx3cnEgR6iCtpz9s62p0fhIgMzFjtBENPZngtmURIMm1ifLPtUIaMhUFn1V519VPmwFIuJcirbM63kYjPhGQxrw/XFcMuTwrDZVvi/Nn9gGHmQVLFqr+AD8A1h/okXFpH8xBmAu3xE8Q6fxOrehpY1AZle8eNos3srGpS7QW7bJ8qI7aI+kegLjqkdmXLfbQ+lfYGptL4Jokqu0M7hQpl4q2Ji3izybVElDbCKyw3OMazee3+BTUd/cEJnnd32qb0shterPWuQ0F+IXnOhm3ga1Jpb6+RgwNNrUJVn5/zwCC3I0WZPOooq0au4P66pGND67ESOntunR9OQ+f36o3wAyqCrcA4tlRu2g6fW1U5FwUqQjKnGpV7koa7qKVjsE9nr4d20b7IQIzCBa5C/AqSfUsnf781QpiFOfT6gRkpqqLrdt3o2KJ4/ZNP3s9cnIyriRM29lGAEbxqeOV82f5fSsN9RLavEEI3+u3LB2BGhB3Ep9MjEzoMEK8Mgw/436nxIUxcsn5hNfqfPOxNFto1hoqgSnTkdAhk+RWKxLM966QNQvokpyCJ4weiszuDWKHVFc+kiDkGpXd1CJT9C defines `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` which sets filter order |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go` | `WithRequestInfo` — parses HTTP URL into structured `RequestInfo` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/request/requestinfo.go` | `RequestInfoFactory.NewRequestInfo` — extracts verb, resource, namespace, name, selectors from URL |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go` | `WithAuthentication` — authenticates request, sets `user.Info` on context |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation.go` | `WithImpersonation` — authorizes and processes impersonation headers before main authz |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go` | `WithAudit` — audit event lifecycle around request handling |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go` | `WithAuthorization` — authorization filter; assembles `AttributesRecord`, calls authorizer chain |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go` | Core interfaces: `Authorizer`, `Attributes`, `AttributesRecord`, `Decision` enum |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer/rule.go` | `ResourceRuleInfo` / `NonResourceRuleInfo` interface definitions |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go` | `unionAuthzHandler` — chains multiple authorizers; short-circuit on Allow/Deny |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizerfactory/builtin.go` | `alwaysAllowAuthorizer`, `alwaysDenyAuthorizer`, `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizerfactory/delegating.go` | `DelegatingAuthorizerConfig` — constructs webhook authorizer for delegated auth |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/path/path.go` | Path-based allow-list authorizer for non-resource endpoints |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/metrics/metrics.go` | `instrumentedAuthorizer` — wraps each authorizer to emit decision metrics |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authentication/user/user.go` | `user.Info` interface and `DefaultInfo` struct; well-known group constants |\n| `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go` | `Config.New` — constructs RBAC/Node/ABAC/Webhook authorizers from configuration |\n| `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go` | `reloadableAuthorizerResolver` — hot-reloads authorizer config; `newForConfig` assembles chain |\n| `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go` | `RBACAuthorizer.Authorize`, `RuleAllows`, `authorizingVisitor` |\n| `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go` | `SubjectAccessEvaluator.AllowedSubjects` — reverse-lookup of subjects for an action |\n| `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/policy.go` | Default cluster roles and bindings installed at cluster bootstrap |\n| `pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go` | `DefaultRuleResolver` — resolves roles/bindings to `PolicyRule` lists; `ConfirmNoEscalation` |\n\n---\n\n## Entry Points\n\n### 1. API Request Entry Points\n\n**Primary HTTP entry point:** Every inbound API request flows through the handler chain built by `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go:1004`. The chain is constructed in reverse; at runtime filters execute in this order:\n\n1. `WithPanicRecovery` / `WithAuditInit`\n2. `WithRequestInfo` — parses the URL path into structured fields\n3. `WithAuthentication` — establishes identity\n4. `WithAudit` — begins audit event\n5. `WithImpersonation` — may substitute identity\n6. Priority/Fairness or MaxInFlight throttling\n7. `WithAuthorization` — makes the final Allow/Deny decision\n8. API handler (the authorized business logic)\n\n**Untrusted inputs entering the URL-parsing stage** (`request/requestinfo.go:RequestInfoFactory.NewRequestInfo`):\n- HTTP method, URL path, query parameters (`fieldSelector`, `labelSelector`, `watch`)\n- These directly populate `RequestInfo.{Verb, Resource, Namespace, Name, Subresource, FieldSelector, LabelSelector}`\n\n**Untrusted inputs entering the authentication stage** (`filters/authentication.go`):\n- `Authorization` HTTP header (Bearer tokens, Basic auth)\n- Client TLS certificates (x509 authenticator)\n- `X-Remote-User`, `X-Remote-Group`, `X-Remote-Extra-*` headers (proxy authenticator — see mitigations below)\n\n**Untrusted inputs entering the impersonation stage** (`filters/impersonation.go`):\n- `Impersonate-User`, `Impersonate-Group`, `Impersonate-Uid`, `Impersonate-Extra-*` HTTP headers\n- Each impersonation request is separately authorized before the identity is substituted\n\n### 2. RBAC Policy Data Entry Points\n\nRBAC policy objects (Roles, ClusterRoles, RoleBindings, ClusterRoleBindings) enter the authorization path through the **shared informer cache**:\n\n- `rbac.RoleGetter` wraps `rbaclisters.RoleLister` (in-memory informer cache)\n- `rbac.RoleBindingLister` wraps `rbaclisters.RoleBindingLister`\n- `rbac.ClusterRoleGetter` wraps `rbaclisters.ClusterRoleLister`\n- `rbac.ClusterRoleBindingLister` wraps `rbaclisters.ClusterRoleBindingLister`\n\nThese are passed into `rbac.New()` at `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go:123`. The authorizer **never reads etcd directly** during authorization; it reads the in-memory reflector cache. Policy changes reach the cache asynchronously via the watch stream.\n\n**Authorization configuration file** (`pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go:163` — `LoadAndValidateFile`): The authorizer chain itself can be hot-reloaded from a YAML file on disk, read and parsed every minute by `runReload` (`reload.go:185`).\n\n### 3. Untrusted Input in Authorization Decisions\n\n| Input | Path | Risk |\n|-------|------|------|\n| URL path & verb | `NewRequestInfo` → `AttributesRecord` | Determines what resource/action is being authorized |\n| User identity (name, groups) | Authenticator → `user.Info` on context | Determines which bindings apply |\n| `X-Remote-User` / `X-Remote-Group` headers | Proxy authenticator → `user.Info` | Spoofable if front-proxy cert validation is misconfigured |\n| Impersonation headers | `buildImpersonationRequests` → authorized substitution | Can change effective identity if impersonation RBAC is too permissive |\n| Label/field selectors | `requestinfo.go` → `AttributesRecord` (feature-gated) | Used in authorization with `AuthorizeWithSelectors` feature gate |\n| Authorization config YAML file | `checkFile` / `LoadAndValidateData` | Config hot-reload path; file on disk must be protected |\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow\n\n### Stage 1 — Request Arrival\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go`\n**Function:** `WithRequestInfo(handler http.Handler, resolver request.RequestInfoResolver) http.Handler`\n\nThe raw `http.Request` is parsed by `RequestInfoFactory.NewRequestInfo`. The result is a `request.RequestInfo` struct stored on the request context via `request.WithRequestInfo(ctx, info)`.\n\n**Data structure: `request.RequestInfo`** (`request/requestinfo.go:44`):\n```\nIsResourceRequest bool\nPath, Verb, APIPrefix, APIGroup, APIVersion string\nNamespace, Resource, Subresource, Name string\nParts []string\nFieldSelector, LabelSelector string\n```\n\nThe verb is translated from HTTP method to Kubernetes verb (e.g., GET → get/list/watch, POST → create). The namespace, resource type, and object name are extracted from the URL path structure (e.g., `/api/v1/namespaces/default/pods/mypod`).\n\n### Stage 2 — Authentication\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`\n**Function:** `withAuthentication(handler, auth authenticator.Request, failed, apiAuds, requestHeaderConfig, metrics)`\n\nThe union `authenticator.Request` is invoked: `resp, ok, err := auth.AuthenticateRequest(req)`.\n\nOn success:\n- Audience validation is performed (`audiencesAreAcceptable`)\n- The `Authorization` header is deleted from the request (`req.Header.Del(\"Authorization\")`)\n- Standard and custom proxy headers (`X-Remote-User`, `X-Remote-Group`, `X-Remote-Extra-*`, `X-Remote-Uid`) are **cleared** via `headerrequest.ClearAuthenticationHeaders`\n- The authenticated `user.Info` is stored on context: `genericapirequest.WithUser(req.Context(), resp.User)`\n- Anonymous HTTP/2 connections receive `Connection: close` (CVE-2023-44487 mitigation)\n\n**Data structure: `user.Info`** (`authentication/user/user.go:20`):\n```\nGetName() string       // e.g., \"system:serviceaccount:default:mysa\"\nGetUID() string\nGetGroups() []string   // e.g., [\"system:authenticated\", \"devs\"]\nGetExtra() map[string][]string\n```\n\nOn failure: the `failedHandler` returns HTTP 401. Failed authentication is also emitted to the audit backend via `WithFailedAuthenticationAudit`.\n\n### Stage 3 — Impersonation Filter\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation.go`\n**Function:** `WithImpersonation(handler, a authorizer.Authorizer, s runtime.NegotiatedSerializer)`\n\nThis filter runs **before** `WithAuthorization`. It reads impersonation headers and, for each target identity component (User, Group, UID, UserExtra), constructs an `authorizer.AttributesRecord` with verb `\"impersonate\"` and calls `a.Authorize(ctx, actingAsAttributes)`. Only if every component is authorized does the filter replace the user on the context with the new `user.DefaultInfo`.\n\nAfter substitution, all impersonation headers are deleted from the request. The impersonation event is logged to the audit record via `audit.LogImpersonatedUser`.\n\n### Stage 4 — Authorization Filter\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`\n**Function:** `WithAuthorization(handler, auth authorizer.Authorizer, s runtime.NegotiatedSerializer)`\n\n**Step 4a — Attribute assembly** via `GetAuthorizerAttributes(ctx)`:\n- Reads `user.Info` from context (set by authentication/impersonation stages)\n- Reads `RequestInfo` from context (set by `WithRequestInfo`)\n- Optionally parses field/label selectors (when `AuthorizeWithSelectors` feature gate is enabled)\n- Constructs `authorizer.AttributesRecord`\n\n**Data structure: `authorizer.AttributesRecord`** (`authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go:104`):\n```\nUser            user.Info\nVerb            string  // get, list, watch, create, update, patch, delete, proxy, ...\nNamespace       string\nAPIGroup        string\nAPIVersion      string\nResource        string\nSubresource     string\nName            string\nResourceRequest bool\nPath            string\nFieldSelectorRequirements fields.Requirements\nLabelSelectorRequirements labels.Requirements\n```\n\n**Step 4b — Authorization decision**: `authorized, reason, err := a.Authorize(ctx, attributes)`\n\nThe result is of type `authorizer.Decision` (an int):\n- `DecisionAllow` (1): request proceeds, audit annotation `authorization.k8s.io/decision: allow`\n- `DecisionDeny` (2): HTTP 403, audit annotation `authorization.k8s.io/decision: forbid`\n- `DecisionNoOpinion` (0): treated as deny by the filter (HTTP 403)\n\n### Stage 4 (inner) — RBAC Evaluation\n\n**File:** `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`\n**Function:** `RBACAuthorizer.Authorize(ctx, requestAttributes authorizer.Attributes)`\n\nThe RBAC authorizer uses a visitor pattern. An `authorizingVisitor` is passed to `VisitRulesFor`:\n\n```go\nr.authorizationRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor(ctx, requestAttributes.GetUser(),\n    requestAttributes.GetNamespace(), ruleCheckingVisitor.visit)\n```\n\n**`DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor`** (`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:179`):\n\n1. Lists all `ClusterRoleBinding` objects from the informer cache\n2. For each binding, calls `appliesTo(user, clusterRoleBinding.Subjects, \"\")`:\n   - `UserKind`: exact string match on `user.GetName()`\n   - `GroupKind`: membership check in `user.GetGroups()`\n   - `ServiceAccountKind`: `serviceaccount.MatchesUsername(namespace, name, user.GetName())`\n3. If the user matches, calls `GetRoleReferenceRules(ctx, binding.RoleRef, \"\")` to resolve the referenced `ClusterRole` or `Role` to its `[]rbacv1.PolicyRule`\n4. Passes each `PolicyRule` to the visitor\n5. Repeats for namespace-scoped `RoleBinding` objects (if `namespace != \"\"`)\n\n**`RuleAllows`** (`rbac.go:178`) performs the policy match:\n- Resource requests: checks verb, API group, resource (including subresource), and resource name against wildcard-aware matchers (`VerbMatches`, `APIGroupMatches`, `ResourceMatches`, `ResourceNameMatches`)\n- Non-resource requests: checks verb and URL path against wildcard matchers\n\n**RBAC returns `DecisionNoOpinion` on denial, never `DecisionDeny`.** This is by design: RBAC only allows; it defers to other authorizers or to the final implicit deny.\n\n### Stage 5 — Decision and Audit\n\n**Authorization filter** (`authorization.go:79`):\n- `DecisionAllow`: adds audit annotations, calls the next handler\n- Error without allow: returns HTTP 500\n- Any other outcome: logs the denial, adds audit annotations (`decision: forbid`), calls `responsewriters.Forbidden` (HTTP 403)\n\n**Audit subsystem** (`filters/audit.go:42`, `WithAudit`):\n- Wraps the response writer to capture the HTTP status code\n- Emits `StageRequestReceived` event before the handler runs\n- Emits `StageResponseComplete` (or `StageResponseStarted` for streaming) after completion\n- The authorization decision is recorded as structured annotations on the audit event via `audit.AddAuditAnnotations`\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\nOrdered from request entry to authorization decision:\n\n```\n1.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go\n    DefaultBuildHandlerChain — assembles all filters\n\n2.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go\n    WithRequestInfo → resolver.NewRequestInfo(req)\n\n3.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/request/requestinfo.go\n    RequestInfoFactory.NewRequestInfo — parses URL into RequestInfo\n\n4.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go\n    WithAuthentication → auth.AuthenticateRequest(req)\n    → stores user.Info on context; clears auth headers\n\n5.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go\n    WithAudit — starts audit event\n\n6.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation.go\n    WithImpersonation → buildImpersonationRequests(req.Header)\n    → a.Authorize(ctx, actingAsAttributes) [for each impersonation component]\n    → replaces user on context if authorized\n\n7.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go\n    WithAuthorization → GetAuthorizerAttributes(ctx)\n    → a.Authorize(ctx, attributes)\n\n8.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go\n    unionAuthzHandler.Authorize — iterates authorizer chain\n\n9.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizerfactory/builtin.go\n    privilegedGroupAuthorizer.Authorize — checked first; allows system:masters\n\n10. pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go\n    reloadableAuthorizerResolver → newForConfig → union.New(...)\n    (wraps each sub-authorizer with authorizationmetrics.InstrumentedAuthorizer)\n\n11. plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go\n    RBACAuthorizer.Authorize → authorizingVisitor.visit\n\n12. pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go\n    DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor\n    → clusterRoleBindingLister.ListClusterRoleBindings (informer cache)\n    → appliesTo(user, subjects, namespace)\n    → GetRoleReferenceRules(ctx, roleRef, namespace)\n    → roleGetter.GetRole / clusterRoleGetter.GetClusterRole (informer cache)\n\n13. plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go\n    RuleAllows → rbacv1helpers.VerbMatches / APIGroupMatches / ResourceMatches / ResourceNameMatches\n\n14. staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go\n    Decision → audit annotations → allow or HTTP 403\n```\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Vulnerability Classes\n\n#### 1. Authentication Bypass (Low Risk — Strongly Mitigated)\n\n**X-Remote-User/Group header injection** is a historical Kubernetes attack surface. An attacker who can send requests directly to the API server with spoofed `X-Remote-User` headers could bypass authentication — but only if the request comes from an IP that the API server trusts as a proxy, or if the front-proxy certificate validation is disabled/misconfigured.\n\nMitigation in code: `authentication.go:91–107` calls `headerrequest.ClearAuthenticationHeaders` for both standard (`X-Remote-User`, `X-Remote-Group`, `X-Remote-Extra-*`, `X-Remote-Uid`) and any custom proxy headers **after** authentication succeeds with the _real_ authenticator. Proxy authentication itself requires a mutually-authenticated TLS client certificate matching the configured proxy CA. If the request was not authenticated via the proxy authenticator, the headers are still cleared before passing to the next handler, preventing downstream code from reading them.\n\n#### 2. Privilege Escalation via Impersonation\n\n**Attack scenario:** A user or service account with the `impersonate` verb on `users`, `groups`, or `serviceaccounts` resources can present any identity to the API server, including `system:masters` group membership.\n\n**Code path:** `impersonation.go:117` calls `a.Authorize(ctx, actingAsAttributes)` for each impersonation component. The `actingAsAttributes` uses the **pre-impersonation** real identity of the requestor. If authorized, the new identity (including group membership) is committed to context.\n\n**Residual risk:** If RBAC grants impersonation permissions too broadly — e.g., `verbs: [\"impersonate\"], resources: [\"users\"], resourceNames: []` without restricting the target — an attacker can impersonate arbitrary users. Wildcards in impersonation RBAC rules are particularly dangerous.\n\n**Absence of escalation guardrail at impersonation time:** The impersonation filter does not check whether the impersonated user would have more privileges than the real user. It only verifies the `impersonate` permission. An account with `impersonate` on `groups` and no restriction on `system:masters` could escalate to cluster-admin.\n\n#### 3. Privilege Escalation via RBAC Policy Escalation\n\nThe RBAC admission layer includes `ConfirmNoEscalation` (`rule.go:53`): when a user creates or updates a Role or ClusterRole, the API validates that the resulting rules are a subset of the requesting user's own permissions. This prevents a user from granting themselves permissions they do not already hold via RBAC object manipulation.\n\n**Residual risk:** The check is only as accurate as the rule resolver at admission time. If the shared informer cache has a delayed view of role bindings (stale cache), a user might be able to briefly escalate by racing between binding creation and cache synchronization, though this is highly impractical.\n\n#### 4. Policy Misconfiguration (Medium Risk — Operational)\n\n**Cluster-admin ClusterRoleBinding abuse:** The default bootstrap policy includes a `cluster-admin` ClusterRole bound to `system:masters`. Any certificate issued with `O=system:masters` is unconditionally authorized by the `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` at `reload.go:98` before RBAC is even consulted. This is a hardcoded bypass without audit-level identity granularity.\n\n**Wildcard rules in RBAC:** PolicyRule wildcards (`verbs: [\"*\"]`, `resources: [\"*\"]`, `apiGroups: [\"*\"]`) grant blanket permissions. The `bootstrappolicy` deliberately grants these to `cluster-admin`, but if granted to end-user accounts, they provide full cluster access.\n\n**RoleBinding to ClusterRole:** A RoleBinding can reference a ClusterRole, scoping the cluster-wide role to a single namespace. Conversely, ClusterRoleBindings apply cluster-wide. Misconfiguration (e.g., granting `cluster-admin` as a namespaced RoleBinding) may be less dangerous than intended, but granting it as a ClusterRoleBinding is full cluster compromise.\n\n**Default service account token:** Every pod receives an auto-mounted service account token. The `default` service account in each namespace has no RBAC permissions by default, but if cluster operators have granted broad bindings to `system:authenticated` or to the `default` service account, pod compromise directly yields API access.\n\n#### 5. Authorizer Chain Logic Flaw (Design-Level Consideration)\n\n**RBAC never denies explicitly.** The `RBACAuthorizer.Authorize` method returns `DecisionNoOpinion` on denial (`rbac.go:126`). This means:\n- If RBAC is listed before a Webhook authorizer and RBAC has no matching rule, the request moves to the webhook authorizer, which may allow it.\n- The effective denial only occurs when the union authorizer exhausts all authorizers without an `Allow` or `Deny`, and the filter treats `NoOpinion` as a 403.\n\nIn a chain of `[Node, RBAC, Webhook]`, a request denied by RBAC still reaches the Webhook. If the Webhook is lenient, RBAC's lack of an explicit deny creates an allow path outside RBAC policy. Operators must understand that the chain is ordered and that `NoOpinion` propagates forward.\n\n#### 6. Authorization Config Hot-Reload Attack Surface\n\n`reload.go:185` (`runReload`) polls the authorization config file every minute. If the file on disk is writable by an attacker, they can inject a new authorizer configuration — for example, changing the chain to `AlwaysAllow` mode or inserting a malicious webhook endpoint. The file must be protected with appropriate OS-level permissions.\n\n### Existing Mitigations\n\n| Mitigation | Location | What It Prevents |\n|------------|----------|------------------|\n| Auth header clearing after authentication | `authentication.go:88–108` | Header injection / proxy spoofing |\n| HTTP/2 GOAWAY for anonymous users | `authentication.go:115–120` | CVE-2023-44487 / HTTP/2 DoS |\n| Impersonation requires explicit `impersonate` verb | `impersonation.go:117` | Unauthorized identity substitution |\n| Impersonation headers cleared after substitution | `impersonation.go:173–180` | Stacked impersonation attacks |\n| `ConfirmNoEscalation` at admission | `rule.go:53` | RBAC policy escalation via object manipulation |\n| `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` is prepended to chain | `reload.go:98` | Ensures break-glass access via client certs |\n| Informer cache for role/binding resolution | `rbac.go:199–224` | Avoids per-request etcd reads; provides consistency |\n| Audit annotations on every decision | `authorization.go:80–95` | Forensic trail of allow/deny and reason |\n| `instrumentedAuthorizer` metrics wrapper | `metrics/metrics.go:62` | Per-authorizer decision observability |\n| Authorizer config validation on load | `config.go:163–213` | Prevents malformed config from replacing the chain |\n| `DecisionDeny` short-circuits chain | `union.go:61` | Webhook or Node authorizer can explicitly block |\n\n### Security Boundaries Between Authorization Plugins\n\nThe union authorizer (`union.go`) is the boundary manager. The interaction rules are:\n\n- **`DecisionAllow`**: stops evaluation, request proceeds. The first authorizer to allow wins.\n- **`DecisionDeny`**: stops evaluation, request is rejected immediately. Only Node and Webhook authorizers currently return explicit Deny; RBAC does not.\n- **`DecisionNoOpinion`**: falls through to the next authorizer.\n\nThere is **no explicit isolation** between authorizers — they all receive the same `Attributes` object. A plugin cannot prevent a later plugin from allowing what it declined. The only true veto mechanism is `DecisionDeny`.\n\nThe `system:masters` bypass (`privilegedGroupAuthorizer`) is inserted **before all configured authorizers** in `newForConfig`, meaning even if RBAC or Webhook would deny the request, `system:masters` group membership preempts the check. This is intentional for emergency/bootstrapping scenarios but represents a permanent bypass with no policy-based override.\n\n### Authorizer Chain Interaction (RBAC, Node, Webhook)\n\n**Node authorizer** (`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/node`) is purpose-built for kubelet identity. It uses a dependency graph (Pods → PVs → Secrets/ConfigMaps) to allow a node to only access secrets/configmaps used by pods scheduled on it. It returns explicit `DecisionDeny` for requests to resources a node should not access. The Node authorizer is positioned in the chain before RBAC and can block requests that RBAC might otherwise allow.\n\n**RBAC authorizer** evaluates policy rules from the etcd-backed informer cache. It is purely additive (no explicit deny). It covers the bulk of cluster authorization for human users and service accounts.\n\n**Webhook authorizer** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/authorizer/webhook`) sends a `SubjectAccessReview` to an external HTTPS endpoint. It supports response caching (allow TTL, deny TTL), retry backoff, and CEL-based match conditions to filter which requests reach the webhook. The `FailurePolicy` (NoOpinion or Deny) determines behavior when the webhook is unreachable — a critical operational security decision.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes RBAC authorization subsystem implements a **defense-in-depth, additive-allow model** with a clearly ordered HTTP filter chain. The key security properties are:\n\n1. **Authentication precedes authorization** and headers that could influence identity are purged after authentication, limiting header injection scope.\n\n2. **Impersonation is independently authorized** against the real user's identity before the substituted identity is committed. However, over-broad impersonation RBAC grants remain the most practical privilege escalation path.\n\n3. **RBAC never explicitly denies** — it returns `DecisionNoOpinion`. Explicit denials are only possible from the Node or Webhook authorizers. Operators who expect RBAC to block requests should understand that later authorizers in the chain may grant access if RBAC has no matching rule.\n\n4. **The `system:masters` group is a hardcoded, unconditional bypass** inserted at the front of the authorizer chain. No RBAC policy can block a request from a member of `system:masters`. This group should be treated with the same sensitivity as root credentials.\n\n5. **Policy data is served from an in-memory informer cache** (not direct etcd reads per request), which provides performance and read consistency but introduces a brief window during which RBAC changes may not yet be reflected in authorization decisions.\n\n6. **Audit logging is integrated at multiple points** — authentication failure, impersonation events, and authorization decisions all produce structured audit entries, providing a forensic trail. However, the audit system is optional; if no backend is configured, `WithAudit` degrades to a no-op.\n\n7. **The authorizer chain is hot-reloadable** from a file, which introduces a file-system trust dependency. The reload file must be protected against unauthorized writes.\n\nThe most actionable security risks are:\n- **Misconfigured impersonation RBAC** (widest practical escalation path)\n- **AlwaysAllow mode** enabled inadvertently (complete bypass)\n- **Overly broad wildcard rules** in ClusterRoleBindings targeting `system:authenticated`\n- **Unprotected authorization config file** enabling chain substitution\n- **Stale informer cache** creating a brief inconsistency window after policy changes (low practical risk, no known exploit path)\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":3,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1693,"cache_read_input_tokens":64747,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":1693,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":5,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"ee1bef8e-c8dc-4568-a1a0-ae2085b11fb1","uuid":"0d032d04-43c3-4ce7-b456-0fb4c61113fe"}

`newForConfig` assembles chain |\n| `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go` | `RBACAuthorizer.Authorize`, `RuleAllows`, `authorizingVisitor` |\n| `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/subject_locator.go` | `SubjectAccessEvaluator.AllowedSubjects` — reverse-lookup of subjects for an action |\n| `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/policy.go` | Default cluster roles and bindings installed at cluster bootstrap |\n| `pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go` | `DefaultRuleResolver` — resolves roles/bindings to `PolicyRule` lists; `ConfirmNoEscalation` |\n\n---\n\n## Entry Points\n\n### 1. API Request Entry Points\n\n**Primary HTTP entry point:** Every inbound API request flows through the handler chain built by `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go:1004`. The chain is constructed in reverse; at runtime filters execute in this order:\n\n1. `WithPanicRecovery` / `WithAuditInit`\n2. `WithRequestInfo` — parses the URL path into structured fields\n3. `WithAuthentication` — establishes identity\n4. `WithAudit` — begins audit event\n5. `WithImpersonation` — may substitute identity\n6. Priority/Fairness or MaxInFlight throttling\n7. `WithAuthorization` — makes the final Allow/Deny decision\n8. API handler (the authorized business logic)\n\n**Untrusted inputs entering the URL-parsing stage** (`request/requestinfo.go:RequestInfoFactory.NewRequestInfo`):\n- HTTP method, URL path, query parameters (`fieldSelector`, `labelSelector`, `watch`)\n- These directly populate `RequestInfo.{Verb, Resource, Namespace, Name, Subresource, FieldSelector, LabelSelector}`\n\n**Untrusted inputs entering the authentication stage** (`filters/authentication.go`):\n- `Authorization` HTTP header (Bearer tokens, Basic auth)\n- Client TLS certificates (x509 authenticator)\n- `X-Remote-User`, `X-Remote-Group`, `X-Remote-Extra-*` headers (proxy authenticator — see mitigations below)\n\n**Untrusted inputs entering the impersonation stage** (`filters/impersonation.go`):\n- `Impersonate-User`, `Impersonate-Group`, `Impersonate-Uid`, `Impersonate-Extra-*` HTTP headers\n- Each impersonation request is separately authorized before the identity is substituted\n\n### 2. RBAC Policy Data Entry Points\n\nRBAC policy objects (Roles, ClusterRoles, RoleBindings, ClusterRoleBindings) enter the authorization path through the **shared informer cache**:\n\n- `rbac.RoleGetter` wraps `rbaclisters.RoleLister` (in-memory informer cache)\n- `rbac.RoleBindingLister` wraps `rbaclisters.RoleBindingLister`\n- `rbac.ClusterRoleGetter` wraps `rbaclisters.ClusterRoleLister`\n- `rbac.ClusterRoleBindingLister` wraps `rbaclisters.ClusterRoleBindingLister`\n\nThese are passed into `rbac.New()` at `pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go:123`. The authorizer **never reads etcd directly** during authorization; it reads the in-memory reflector cache. Policy changes reach the cache asynchronously via the watch stream.\n\n**Authorization configuration file** (`pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/config.go:163` — `LoadAndValidateFile`): The authorizer chain itself can be hot-reloaded from a YAML file on disk, read and parsed every minute by `runReload` (`reload.go:185`).\n\n### 3. Untrusted Input in Authorization Decisions\n\n| Input | Path | Risk |\n|-------|------|------|\n| URL path & verb | `NewRequestInfo` → `AttributesRecord` | Determines what resource/action is being authorized |\n| User identity (name, groups) | Authenticator → `user.Info` on context | Determines which bindings apply |\n| `X-Remote-User` / `X-Remote-Group` headers | Proxy authenticator → `user.Info` | Spoofable if front-proxy cert validation is misconfigured |\n| Impersonation headers | `buildImpersonationRequests` → authorized substitution | Can change effective identity if impersonation RBAC is too permissive |\n| Label/field selectors | `requestinfo.go` → `AttributesRecord` (feature-gated) | Used in authorization with `AuthorizeWithSelectors` feature gate |\n| Authorization config YAML file | `checkFile` / `LoadAndValidateData` | Config hot-reload path; file on disk must be protected |\n\n---\n\n## Data Flow\n\n### Stage 1 — Request Arrival\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go`\n**Function:** `WithRequestInfo(handler http.Handler, resolver request.RequestInfoResolver) http.Handler`\n\nThe raw `http.Request` is parsed by `RequestInfoFactory.NewRequestInfo`. The result is a `request.RequestInfo` struct stored on the request context via `request.WithRequestInfo(ctx, info)`.\n\n**Data structure: `request.RequestInfo`** (`request/requestinfo.go:44`):\n```\nIsResourceRequest bool\nPath, Verb, APIPrefix, APIGroup, APIVersion string\nNamespace, Resource, Subresource, Name string\nParts []string\nFieldSelector, LabelSelector string\n```\n\nThe verb is translated from HTTP method to Kubernetes verb (e.g., GET → get/list/watch, POST → create). The namespace, resource type, and object name are extracted from the URL path structure (e.g., `/api/v1/namespaces/default/pods/mypod`).\n\n### Stage 2 — Authentication\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go`\n**Function:** `withAuthentication(handler, auth authenticator.Request, failed, apiAuds, requestHeaderConfig, metrics)`\n\nThe union `authenticator.Request` is invoked: `resp, ok, err := auth.AuthenticateRequest(req)`.\n\nOn success:\n- Audience validation is performed (`audiencesAreAcceptable`)\n- The `Authorization` header is deleted from the request (`req.Header.Del(\"Authorization\")`)\n- Standard and custom proxy headers (`X-Remote-User`, `X-Remote-Group`, `X-Remote-Extra-*`, `X-Remote-Uid`) are **cleared** via `headerrequest.ClearAuthenticationHeaders`\n- The authenticated `user.Info` is stored on context: `genericapirequest.WithUser(req.Context(), resp.User)`\n- Anonymous HTTP/2 connections receive `Connection: close` (CVE-2023-44487 mitigation)\n\n**Data structure: `user.Info`** (`authentication/user/user.go:20`):\n```\nGetName() string       // e.g., \"system:serviceaccount:default:mysa\"\nGetUID() string\nGetGroups() []string   // e.g., [\"system:authenticated\", \"devs\"]\nGetExtra() map[string][]string\n```\n\nOn failure: the `failedHandler` returns HTTP 401. Failed authentication is also emitted to the audit backend via `WithFailedAuthenticationAudit`.\n\n### Stage 3 — Impersonation Filter\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation.go`\n**Function:** `WithImpersonation(handler, a authorizer.Authorizer, s runtime.NegotiatedSerializer)`\n\nThis filter runs **before** `WithAuthorization`. It reads impersonation headers and, for each target identity component (User, Group, UID, UserExtra), constructs an `authorizer.AttributesRecord` with verb `\"impersonate\"` and calls `a.Authorize(ctx, actingAsAttributes)`. Only if every component is authorized does the filter replace the user on the context with the new `user.DefaultInfo`.\n\nAfter substitution, all impersonation headers are deleted from the request. The impersonation event is logged to the audit record via `audit.LogImpersonatedUser`.\n\n### Stage 4 — Authorization Filter\n\n**File:** `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go`\n**Function:** `WithAuthorization(handler, auth authorizer.Authorizer, s runtime.NegotiatedSerializer)`\n\n**Step 4a — Attribute assembly** via `GetAuthorizerAttributes(ctx)`:\n- Reads `user.Info` from context (set by authentication/impersonation stages)\n- Reads `RequestInfo` from context (set by `WithRequestInfo`)\n- Optionally parses field/label selectors (when `AuthorizeWithSelectors` feature gate is enabled)\n- Constructs `authorizer.AttributesRecord`\n\n**Data structure: `authorizer.AttributesRecord`** (`authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go:104`):\n```\nUser            user.Info\nVerb            string  // get, list, watch, create, update, patch, delete, proxy, ...\nNamespace       string\nAPIGroup        string\nAPIVersion      string\nResource        string\nSubresource     string\nName            string\nResourceRequest bool\nPath            string\nFieldSelectorRequirements fields.Requirements\nLabelSelectorRequirements labels.Requirements\n```\n\n**Step 4b — Authorization decision**: `authorized, reason, err := a.Authorize(ctx, attributes)`\n\nThe result is of type `authorizer.Decision` (an int):\n- `DecisionAllow` (1): request proceeds, audit annotation `authorization.k8s.io/decision: allow`\n- `DecisionDeny` (2): HTTP 403, audit annotation `authorization.k8s.io/decision: forbid`\n- `DecisionNoOpinion` (0): treated as deny by the filter (HTTP 403)\n\n### Stage 4 (inner) — RBAC Evaluation\n\n**File:** `plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go`\n**Function:** `RBACAuthorizer.Authorize(ctx, requestAttributes authorizer.Attributes)`\n\nThe RBAC authorizer uses a visitor pattern. An `authorizingVisitor` is passed to `VisitRulesFor`:\n\n```go\nr.authorizationRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor(ctx, requestAttributes.GetUser(),\n    requestAttributes.GetNamespace(), ruleCheckingVisitor.visit)\n```\n\n**`DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor`** (`pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go:179`):\n\n1. Lists all `ClusterRoleBinding` objects from the informer cache\n2. For each binding, calls `appliesTo(user, clusterRoleBinding.Subjects, \"\")`:\n   - `UserKind`: exact string match on `user.GetName()`\n   - `GroupKind`: membership check in `user.GetGroups()`\n   - `ServiceAccountKind`: `serviceaccount.MatchesUsername(namespace, name, user.GetName())`\n3. If the user matches, calls `GetRoleReferenceRules(ctx, binding.RoleRef, \"\")` to resolve the referenced `ClusterRole` or `Role` to its `[]rbacv1.PolicyRule`\n4. Passes each `PolicyRule` to the visitor\n5. Repeats for namespace-scoped `RoleBinding` objects (if `namespace != \"\"`)\n\n**`RuleAllows`** (`rbac.go:178`) performs the policy match:\n- Resource requests: checks verb, API group, resource (including subresource), and resource name against wildcard-aware matchers (`VerbMatches`, `APIGroupMatches`, `ResourceMatches`, `ResourceNameMatches`)\n- Non-resource requests: checks verb and URL path against wildcard matchers\n\n**RBAC returns `DecisionNoOpinion` on denial, never `DecisionDeny`.** This is by design: RBAC only allows; it defers to other authorizers or to the final implicit deny.\n\n### Stage 5 — Decision and Audit\n\n**Authorization filter** (`authorization.go:79`):\n- `DecisionAllow`: adds audit annotations, calls the next handler\n- Error without allow: returns HTTP 500\n- Any other outcome: logs the denial, adds audit annotations (`decision: forbid`), calls `responsewriters.Forbidden` (HTTP 403)\n\n**Audit subsystem** (`filters/audit.go:42`, `WithAudit`):\n- Wraps the response writer to capture the HTTP status code\n- Emits `StageRequestReceived` event before the handler runs\n- Emits `StageResponseComplete` (or `StageResponseStarted` for streaming) after completion\n- The authorization decision is recorded as structured annotations on the audit event via `audit.AddAuditAnnotations`\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\nOrdered from request entry to authorization decision:\n\n```\n1.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go\n    DefaultBuildHandlerChain — assembles all filters\n\n2.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go\n    WithRequestInfo → resolver.NewRequestInfo(req)\n\n3.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/request/requestinfo.go\n    RequestInfoFactory.NewRequestInfo — parses URL into RequestInfo\n\n4.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go\n    WithAuthentication → auth.AuthenticateRequest(req)\n    → stores user.Info on context; clears auth headers\n\n5.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go\n    WithAudit — starts audit event\n\n6.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation.go\n    WithImpersonation → buildImpersonationRequests(req.Header)\n    → a.Authorize(ctx, actingAsAttributes) [for each impersonation component]\n    → replaces user on context if authorized\n\n7.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go\n    WithAuthorization → GetAuthorizerAttributes(ctx)\n    → a.Authorize(ctx, attributes)\n\n8.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/union/union.go\n    unionAuthzHandler.Authorize — iterates authorizer chain\n\n9.  staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizerfactory/builtin.go\n    privilegedGroupAuthorizer.Authorize — checked first; allows system:masters\n\n10. pkg/kubeapiserver/authorizer/reload.go\n    reloadableAuthorizerResolver → newForConfig → union.New(...)\n    (wraps each sub-authorizer with authorizationmetrics.InstrumentedAuthorizer)\n\n11. plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go\n    RBACAuthorizer.Authorize → authorizingVisitor.visit\n\n12. pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go\n    DefaultRuleResolver.VisitRulesFor\n    → clusterRoleBindingLister.ListClusterRoleBindings (informer cache)\n    → appliesTo(user, subjects, namespace)\n    → GetRoleReferenceRules(ctx, roleRef, namespace)\n    → roleGetter.GetRole / clusterRoleGetter.GetClusterRole (informer cache)\n\n13. plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/rbac.go\n    RuleAllows → rbacv1helpers.VerbMatches / APIGroupMatches / ResourceMatches / ResourceNameMatches\n\n14. staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go\n    Decision → audit annotations → allow or HTTP 403\n```\n\n---\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Vulnerability Classes\n\n#### 1. Authentication Bypass (Low Risk — Strongly Mitigated)\n\n**X-Remote-User/Group header injection** is a historical Kubernetes attack surface. An attacker who can send requests directly to the API server with spoofed `X-Remote-User` headers could bypass authentication — but only if the request comes from an IP that the API server trusts as a proxy, or if the front-proxy certificate validation is disabled/misconfigured.\n\nMitigation in code: `authentication.go:91–107` calls `headerrequest.ClearAuthenticationHeaders` for both standard (`X-Remote-User`, `X-Remote-Group`, `X-Remote-Extra-*`, `X-Remote-Uid`) and any custom proxy headers **after** authentication succeeds with the _real_ authenticator. Proxy authentication itself requires a mutually-authenticated TLS client certificate matching the configured proxy CA. If the request was not authenticated via the proxy authenticator, the headers are still cleared before passing to the next handler, preventing downstream code from reading them.\n\n#### 2. Privilege Escalation via Impersonation\n\n**Attack scenario:** A user or service account with the `impersonate` verb on `users`, `groups`, or `serviceaccounts` resources can present any identity to the API server, including `system:masters` group membership.\n\n**Code path:** `impersonation.go:117` calls `a.Authorize(ctx, actingAsAttributes)` for each impersonation component. The `actingAsAttributes` uses the **pre-impersonation** real identity of the requestor. If authorized, the new identity (including group membership) is committed to context.\n\n**Residual risk:** If RBAC grants impersonation permissions too broadly — e.g., `verbs: [\"impersonate\"], resources: [\"users\"], resourceNames: []` without restricting the target — an attacker can impersonate arbitrary users. Wildcards in impersonation RBAC rules are particularly dangerous.\n\n**Absence of escalation guardrail at impersonation time:** The impersonation filter does not check whether the impersonated user would have more privileges than the real user. It only verifies the `impersonate` permission. An account with `impersonate` on `groups` and no restriction on `system:masters` could escalate to cluster-admin.\n\n#### 3. Privilege Escalation via RBAC Policy Escalation\n\nThe RBAC admission layer includes `ConfirmNoEscalation` (`rule.go:53`): when a user creates or updates a Role or ClusterRole, the API validates that the resulting rules are a subset of the requesting user's own permissions. This prevents a user from granting themselves permissions they do not already hold via RBAC object manipulation.\n\n**Residual risk:** The check is only as accurate as the rule resolver at admission time. If the shared informer cache has a delayed view of role bindings (stale cache), a user might be able to briefly escalate by racing between binding creation and cache synchronization, though this is highly impractical.\n\n#### 4. Policy Misconfiguration (Medium Risk — Operational)\n\n**Cluster-admin ClusterRoleBinding abuse:** The default bootstrap policy includes a `cluster-admin` ClusterRole bound to `system:masters`. Any certificate issued with `O=system:masters` is unconditionally authorized by the `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` at `reload.go:98` before RBAC is even consulted. This is a hardcoded bypass without audit-level identity granularity.\n\n**Wildcard rules in RBAC:** PolicyRule wildcards (`verbs: [\"*\"]`, `resources: [\"*\"]`, `apiGroups: [\"*\"]`) grant blanket permissions. The `bootstrappolicy` deliberately grants these to `cluster-admin`, but if granted to end-user accounts, they provide full cluster access.\n\n**RoleBinding to ClusterRole:** A RoleBinding can reference a ClusterRole, scoping the cluster-wide role to a single namespace. Conversely, ClusterRoleBindings apply cluster-wide. Misconfiguration (e.g., granting `cluster-admin` as a namespaced RoleBinding) may be less dangerous than intended, but granting it as a ClusterRoleBinding is full cluster compromise.\n\n**Default service account token:** Every pod receives an auto-mounted service account token. The `default` service account in each namespace has no RBAC permissions by default, but if cluster operators have granted broad bindings to `system:authenticated` or to the `default` service account, pod compromise directly yields API access.\n\n#### 5. Authorizer Chain Logic Flaw (Design-Level Consideration)\n\n**RBAC never denies explicitly.** The `RBACAuthorizer.Authorize` method returns `DecisionNoOpinion` on denial (`rbac.go:126`). This means:\n- If RBAC is listed before a Webhook authorizer and RBAC has no matching rule, the request moves to the webhook authorizer, which may allow it.\n- The effective denial only occurs when the union authorizer exhausts all authorizers without an `Allow` or `Deny`, and the filter treats `NoOpinion` as a 403.\n\nIn a chain of `[Node, RBAC, Webhook]`, a request denied by RBAC still reaches the Webhook. If the Webhook is lenient, RBAC's lack of an explicit deny creates an allow path outside RBAC policy. Operators must understand that the chain is ordered and that `NoOpinion` propagates forward.\n\n#### 6. Authorization Config Hot-Reload Attack Surface\n\n`reload.go:185` (`runReload`) polls the authorization config file every minute. If the file on disk is writable by an attacker, they can inject a new authorizer configuration — for example, changing the chain to `AlwaysAllow` mode or inserting a malicious webhook endpoint. The file must be protected with appropriate OS-level permissions.\n\n### Existing Mitigations\n\n| Mitigation | Location | What It Prevents |\n|------------|----------|------------------|\n| Auth header clearing after authentication | `authentication.go:88–108` | Header injection / proxy spoofing |\n| HTTP/2 GOAWAY for anonymous users | `authentication.go:115–120` | CVE-2023-44487 / HTTP/2 DoS |\n| Impersonation requires explicit `impersonate` verb | `impersonation.go:117` | Unauthorized identity substitution |\n| Impersonation headers cleared after substitution | `impersonation.go:173–180` | Stacked impersonation attacks |\n| `ConfirmNoEscalation` at admission | `rule.go:53` | RBAC policy escalation via object manipulation |\n| `privilegedGroupAuthorizer` is prepended to chain | `reload.go:98` | Ensures break-glass access via client certs |\n| Informer cache for role/binding resolution | `rbac.go:199–224` | Avoids per-request etcd reads; provides consistency |\n| Audit annotations on every decision | `authorization.go:80–95` | Forensic trail of allow/deny and reason |\n| `instrumentedAuthorizer` metrics wrapper | `metrics/metrics.go:62` | Per-authorizer decision observability |\n| Authorizer config validation on load | `config.go:163–213` | Prevents malformed config from replacing the chain |\n| `DecisionDeny` short-circuits chain | `union.go:61` | Webhook or Node authorizer can explicitly block |\n\n### Security Boundaries Between Authorization Plugins\n\nThe union authorizer (`union.go`) is the boundary manager. The interaction rules are:\n\n- **`DecisionAllow`**: stops evaluation, request proceeds. The first authorizer to allow wins.\n- **`DecisionDeny`**: stops evaluation, request is rejected immediately. Only Node and Webhook authorizers currently return explicit Deny; RBAC does not.\n- **`DecisionNoOpinion`**: falls through to the next authorizer.\n\nThere is **no explicit isolation** between authorizers — they all receive the same `Attributes` object. A plugin cannot prevent a later plugin from allowing what it declined. The only true veto mechanism is `DecisionDeny`.\n\nThe `system:masters` bypass (`privilegedGroupAuthorizer`) is inserted **before all configured authorizers** in `newForConfig`, meaning even if RBAC or Webhook would deny the request, `system:masters` group membership preempts the check. This is intentional for emergency/bootstrapping scenarios but represents a permanent bypass with no policy-based override.\n\n### Authorizer Chain Interaction (RBAC, Node, Webhook)\n\n**Node authorizer** (`plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/node`) is purpose-built for kubelet identity. It uses a dependency graph (Pods → PVs → Secrets/ConfigMaps) to allow a node to only access secrets/configmaps used by pods scheduled on it. It returns explicit `DecisionDeny` for requests to resources a node should not access. The Node authorizer is positioned in the chain before RBAC and can block requests that RBAC might otherwise allow.\n\n**RBAC authorizer** evaluates policy rules from the etcd-backed informer cache. It is purely additive (no explicit deny). It covers the bulk of cluster authorization for human users and service accounts.\n\n**Webhook authorizer** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/plugin/pkg/authorizer/webhook`) sends a `SubjectAccessReview` to an external HTTPS endpoint. It supports response caching (allow TTL, deny TTL), retry backoff, and CEL-based match conditions to filter which requests reach the webhook. The `FailurePolicy` (NoOpinion or Deny) determines behavior when the webhook is unreachable — a critical operational security decision.\n\n---\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes RBAC authorization subsystem implements a **defense-in-depth, additive-allow model** with a clearly ordered HTTP filter chain. The key security properties are:\n\n1. **Authentication precedes authorization** and headers that could influence identity are purged after authentication, limiting header injection scope.\n\n2. **Impersonation is independently authorized** against the real user's identity before the substituted identity is committed. However, over-broad impersonation RBAC grants remain the most practical privilege escalation path.\n\n3. **RBAC never explicitly denies** — it returns `DecisionNoOpinion`. Explicit denials are only possible from the Node or Webhook authorizers. Operators who expect RBAC to block requests should understand that later authorizers in the chain may grant access if RBAC has no matching rule.\n\n4. **The `system:masters` group is a hardcoded, unconditional bypass** inserted at the front of the authorizer chain. No RBAC policy can block a request from a member of `system:masters`. This group should be treated with the same sensitivity as root credentials.\n\n5. **Policy data is served from an in-memory informer cache** (not direct etcd reads per request), which provides performance and read consistency but introduces a brief window during which RBAC changes may not yet be reflected in authorization decisions.\n\n6. **Audit logging is integrated at multiple points** — authentication failure, impersonation events, and authorization decisions all produce structured audit entries, providing a forensic trail. However, the audit system is optional; if no backend is configured, `WithAudit` degrades to a no-op.\n\n7. **The authorizer chain is hot-reloadable** from a file, which introduces a file-system trust dependency. The reload file must be protected against unauthorized writes.\n\nThe most actionable security risks are:\n- **Misconfigured impersonation RBAC** (widest practical escalation path)\n- **AlwaysAllow mode** enabled inadvertently (complete bypass)\n- **Overly broad wildcard rules** in ClusterRoleBindings targeting `system:authenticated`\n- **Unprotected authorization config file** enabling chain substitution\n- **Stale informer cache** creating a brief inconsistency window after policy changes (low practical risk, no known exploit path)\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
